# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Firefox SpiderMonkey JS Parsing to Bytecode Chain

## Your Task

Trace how JavaScript source text is parsed and compiled to bytecode in mozilla/gecko-dev SpiderMonkey. Find C++ source files implementing: the JS parser entry point, the AST node types, the bytecode emitter, and the JSScript bytecode output.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossrepo domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/firefox--871325b8.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/firefox--871325b8` (mozilla-firefox/firefox)

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [

  ],

}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

Perfect! I've created a comprehensive analysis of the SpiderMonkey JavaScript parsing to bytecode compilation chain. Here's a summary of what I found:

## SpiderMonkey Compilation Pipeline

The JavaScript source-to-bytecode chain consists of these key stages:

### **1. Entry Point**
- **`CompileGlobalScript()`** (js/src/frontend/BytecodeCompiler.h) - The main API for compilation

### **2. Lexical Analysis**
- **`TokenStream`** (js/src/frontend/TokenStream.h/cpp) - Converts source text into tokens

### **3. Parsing**
- **`Parser<FullParseHandler, Unit>::globalBody()`** (js/src/frontend/Parser.cpp:1867) - Parses tokens and builds AST

### **4. AST Representation**  
- **`ParseNode`** and 100+ subclasses (js/src/frontend/ParseNode.h) - Abstract syntax tree node types
- Includes UnaryNode, BinaryNode, FunctionNode, and many domain-specific nodes

### **5. Bytecode Emission**
- **`BytecodeEmitter`** (js/src/frontend/BytecodeEmitter.h/cpp)
- **`emitScript()`** (js/src/frontend/BytecodeEmitter.cpp:2354) - Traverses AST and generates bytecode

### **6. Bytecode Instructions**
- **`JSOp`** enum (js/src/vm/Opcodes.h) - Defines all VM opcodes with specifications

### **7. Bytecode Output**
- **`JSScript`** class (js/src/vm/JSScript.h/cpp)
- **`JSScript::Create()`** (js/src/vm/JSScript.cpp:2526) - Creates executable bytecode script objects

The answer has been saved to `/workspace/answer.json` with complete file paths, symbol locations, and a detailed narrative explaining the entire pipeline.

This is information conceptually \\\"passed down\\\"\\n53:  * into parsing sub-nodes. This helps determine which bindings are closed-over, which affects\\n66:  * how they're stored; and whether special bindings like `this` and `arguments`\\n67:  * can be optimized away.\\n68:  *\\n69:  * ParseContext.h: class ParseContext: Extremely complex class that serves a lot\\n70:  * of purposes, but it's a single class - essentially no derived classes - so\\n71:  * it's a little easier to comprehend all at once. You may push to this stack via calling the\\n77:  * constructor with a GeneralParser as an argument (usually `this`), which\\n78:  * pushes itself onto `this->pc` (so it does get assigned/pushed, even though no\\n79:  * assignment ever appears directly in the parser)\\n80:  *\\n81:  * ParseContext contains a pointer to a SharedContext.\\n82:  *\\n83:  * There's a decent chunk of flags/data collection in here too, some \\\"pass-down\\\"\\n84:  * data and some \\\"return-up\\\" data.\\n85:  *\\n86:  * ParseContext also contains a significant number of *sub*-Nestables as fields\\n87:  * of itself (nestables inside nestables). The sub-nestables are:\\n90:  *\\n91:  * ParseContext::Statement: stack of statements.\\n92:  * `if (x) { while (true) { try { ..stack of [if, while, try].. } ... } }`\\n93:  *\\n94:  * It calls the parser, bytecode emitter, etc.\n36:  *\n37:  * ParseContext.h and SharedContext.h: Both have similar purposes. They're split\n38:  * because ParseContext contains information used only by the parser, and\n39:  * SharedContext contains information used by both the parser and\n40:  * BytecodeEmitter.\n41:  *\n42:  * SharedContext.h: class Directives: this contains boolean flags for tracking\n43:  * if we're in asm.js or \"use strict\" code. The \"use strict\" bit is stored in\n44:  * SharedContext, and additionally, the full Directives class is stored in\n45:  * ParseContext - if a direcive is encountered while parsing, this is updated,\n46:  * and checked in GeneralParser::functionDefinition, and if it changed, the\n47:  * whole function is re-parsed with the new flags.\n48:  *\n49:  * SharedContext.h: abstract class SharedContext: This class contains two\n50:  * different groups of flags:\n51:  *\n52:  * Parse context information. This is information conceptually \"passed down\"\n53:  * into parsing sub-nodes. This is like \"are we parsing strict code?\", and so\n54:  * the parser can make decisions of how to parse based off that.\n55:  *\n56:  * Gathered-while-parsing information. This is information conceptually\n57:  * \"returned up\" from parsing sub-nodes. This is like \"did we see a use strict\n58:  * directive\"?\n59:  *\n60:  * Additionally, subclasses (GlobalSharedContext, ModuleSharedContext,\n61:  * EvalSharedContext, and FunctionBox) contain binding information, scope\n62:  * information, and other such bits of data.\n63:  *\n64:  * ParseContext.h: class UsedNameTracker: Track which bindings are used in which\n65:  * scopes. This helps determine which bindings are closed-over, which affects\n66:  * how they're stored; and whether special bindings like `this` and `arguments`\n67:  * can be optimized away.\n68:  *\n69:  * ParseContext.h: class ParseContext: Extremely complex class that serves a lot\n70:  * of purposes, but it's a single class - essentially no derived classes - so\n71:  * it's a little easier to comprehend all at once. (SourceParseContext does\n72:  * derive from ParseContext, but they does nothing except adjust the\n73:  * constructor's arguments).\n74:  * Note it uses a thing called Nestable, which implements a stack of objects:\n75:  * you can push (and pop) instances to a stack (linked list) as you parse\n76:  * further into the parse tree. You may push to this stack via calling the\n77:  * constructor with a GeneralParser as an argument (usually `this`), which\n78:  * pushes itself onto `this->pc` (so it does get assigned/pushed, even though no\n79:  * assignment ever appears directly in the parser)\n80:  *\n81:  * ParseContext contains a pointer to a SharedContext.\n82:  *\n83:  * There's a decent chunk of flags/data collection in here too, some \"pass-down\"\n84:  * data and some \"return-up\" data.\n85:  *\n86:  * ParseContext also contains a significant number of *sub*-Nestables as fields\n87:  * of itself (nestables inside nestables). Note you also push/pop to these via\n88:  * passing `Parser->pc`, which the constructor of the sub-nestable knows which\n89:  * ParseContext field to push to. The sub-nestables are:\n90:  *\n91:  * ParseContext::Statement: stack of statements.\n92:  * `if (x) { while (true) { try { ..stack of [if, while, try].. } ... } }`\n93:  *\n94:  * ParseContext::LabelStatement: interspersed in Statement stack, for labeled\n95:  * statements, for e.g. `label: while (true) { break label; }`\n96:  *\n97:  * ParseContext::ClassStatement: interspersed in Statement stack, for classes\n98:  * the parser is currently inside of.\n99:  *\n100:  * ParseContext::Scope: Set of variables in each scope (stack of sets):\n101:  * `{ let a; let b; { let c; } }`\n102:  * (this gets complicated with `var`, etc., check the class for docs)\n103:  */\n104: \n105: class JSFunction;\n106: class JSObject;\n107: class JSScript;\n108: struct TDZCheckCache is a cache to optimize away unnecessary TDZ check\n133: // operations.\n134: //\n135: // See comments for TDZCheckCache for more details.\n136: //\n137: //\n138: // Control structures\n139: // ------------------\n140: //\n141: // # Jump list\n142: //\n143: // When emitting jump-related bytecode (if-else, break/continue, try-catch),\n144: // forward jump is tracked by JumpList class, in order to patch the jump\n145: // after the jump target is emitted.\n146: //\n147: // See the comment above JumpList class for mode details.\n148: //\n149: //\n150: // # Loop and label\n151: ",
